Summary 164:
Jurisdiction and judicial cooperation in civil matters — EU rules on judicial cooperation and service of judicial documents
JUDICIAL cooperation and services
SUMMARY OF:
Decision (EU) 2016/852 — rules on the transmission and delivery of judicial and postal documents
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE DECISION?
It aims to improve judicial cooperation between EU countries’ judicial authorities in the field of civil matters.
KEY POINTS
The decision adopts Regulation (EC) No 852/2014 on the EU’s cooperation with the European Convention on the Administration of Justice in Civil Matters (ECATC).
The aim of the decision is to establish an area of judicial cooperation where EU countries are required to cooperate in order to ensure the proper functioning of the internal market.
The regulation applies to:
judicial documents;
postal services;
telecommunications and postal services.
It does not apply to service by diplomatic or consular agents, service by postal services and direct service.
FROM WHEN DOES THIS DECISION APPLY?
 
It has applied since 1 July 2016.
BACKGROUND
   
For more information, see:
‘EU judicial cooperation’ on the European Commission's website.
* KEY TERMS
* Judicial cooperation: the cooperation of EU countries in the administration of justice.
MAIN DOCUMENTS
* Requests for judicial documents: requests for the transmission, receipt or service of documents by a judicial or postal service or by a receiving agency.
REFERENCodes: a request for a judicial document to be transmitted, received or transmitted by an EU country.
Transmission of documents: a document to which a court has granted a right of access.
Receipts: the transmission of documents to a court.
Direct service: the transfer of documents from one EU country to another.
EU countries may refuse to provide direct service to a person who is a national of another EU country or who is not resident in the EU country in which the request for service is made.
Requests for service include:
a request for the transmitting agency to provide a copy of the document to the court;
request for the receiving agency to send a copy to the defendant;
the receipt of a copy by the defendant.
In addition, requests for service may be refused if:
the transmitting agency considers that service is not feasible within a reasonable period of time;
there is a risk that the document will be destroyed, destroyed or damaged;
it is likely that the person concerned will not be able to produce the document in a timely manner; or
the person concerned has not been able to prove his or her innocence in the case of a criminal offence.
When a request is refused, the requesting agency must inform the defendant of the reasons for its refusal.
Where a request to provide service is refused by a transmitting agency, the defendant must be informed of the reason for the refusal and of the conditions under which service is possible. The transmitting agency must also provide the defendant with all the necessary information, such as the name of the person who made the request, the date of the request and the reason why the request was refused.
If a defendant does not appear before a court, he or she is entitled to a judgment.
Defendants not entering an appearance may be held liable for a fine of up to €10,000 for each day that they are not present at the court. EU countries must communicate this fixed fee to the Commission.
WHEN DOES THE DIRECTIVE APPLIE?
From 1 July 2018.
For further information, please consult:
EU Judicial Cooperation (European Commission).
KEY TERM
* Communication from the Commission to the European Parliament, the Council, the European Economic and Social Committee and the Committee of the Regions: a communication on the application of the EU Treaty on the Functioning of the European Union (TFEU).
ACT
Council Decision (EU, Euratom) 2016 /852 of 29 June 2016 on the rules on transmission and service (OJ L 183, 30.6.2016, pp. 1-2)
RELATED DOCUMENT
  (EU-wide)
Council Directive (EU), Euratom of 29 May 2014 on the implementation of the Treaty on European Union on the Agreement between the European Community and the European Atomic Energy Community on the Organisation for Economic Cooperation and Development on the Association of States of the one part, and the United Nations Economic Commission for Europe on the Organization for Security and Co-operation in Europe, on the other part.
last update 14.02.2018



Summary 165:
EU rules on advanced therapy medicinal products for the treatment of diseases and dysfunctions of the human body (until 31 December 2020)
EU rules governing advanced therapy medicines for the use of humans
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 726/2004 on the marketing of advanced therapies
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It lays down rules for the marketing, labelling and approval of medicinal products designed to treat diseases and disorders caused by cells or tissues derived from cells or tissue.
It aims to encourage the development of new therapies to treat these diseases and to improve the quality of life of patients.
KEY POINTS
  
The regulation applies to medicinal products intended for use in the EU. These products may be used to treat any of the following conditions:
cancer;
diabetes;
cancer of the central nervous system;
dysfunction of the brain;
sickness;
musculo-skeletal disorders;
degenerative disorders.
The legislation does not apply to:
tuberculosis;
parasitic disorders; and
certain forms of cancer.
Manufacturers must ensure that:
patients are informed of the medicinal product before they receive it;
the medicinal product is used;
there is a risk of adverse reactions to the product;
it has been tested on animals and humans;
in the case of rare diseases, the product is not suitable for human use.
the patient is informed of any adverse reactions.
EU countries must establish and maintain a system for patient and product traceability.
In addition, EU countries must:
ensure that the competent authorities in their respective EU countries have the necessary information on the medicinal products;
establish and maintain an inventory of all medicinal products in their territory;
monitor the clinical trials;
identify and monitor the use and the adverse reactions of patients;
provide the competent authority with information on adverse reactions;
assess the safety and efficacy of the product and the risks to human health;
check that the product has not been used on animals, humans or the environment;
keep a register of all adverse reactions, reactions and adverse reactions that have been reported;
report to the European Medicines Agency (EMA) any adverse reaction to a medicinal product and any other adverse reactions or adverse reactions they may have had;
draw up a draft opinion on the medical use of an advanced therapy product. The draft opinion must mention the divergent positions and the grounds on which they are based.
An EU country must also ensure that the hospital, institution or private practice where the advanced therapy medicine is used has the necessary documentation and that the patient and products are traceable.
A committee for advanced therapy is set up by Regulation (EU) 2019/852 to ensure the proper functioning of the committee.
FROM WHEN DOES THIS REGULATE APPLY?
 
It has applied since 1 December 2004.
BACKGROUND
ACT
Commission Directive 2007/47/EC of 29 June 2007 on the approval, marketing and authorisation of advanced therapeutic medicinal products (OJ L 183, 31.7.2007, pp. 1-8)
RELATED ACTS
  (1) Regulation (European Parliament and of the Council) No 852/2006 on the Medicinal Products for Human Use (MPA-H) (Official Journal L 94, 30.6.2006)
Directive 2009/33/EC on the harmonisation of the laws of the Member States relating to the manufacture, presentation and marketing of medicines and medical devices intended for human uses (Official Code of Practice).
last update 14.02.2020



Summary 166:
EU type approval for motor vehicles
European type approval system
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 596/2010 — type approval of motor vehicles and their trailers
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It aims to ensure that the European Union (EU) type-approval system applies to all types of vehicles, regardless of their make and type.
It also aims to improve the environmental performance of these vehicles.
KEY POINTS
Type approval
EU countries must ensure that type approval is carried out in accordance with the requirements laid down in Regulation (EC, Euratom) No 852/2004 on the harmonisation of the laws of the Member States relating to type approval.
The regulation applies to:
motor vehicles, their trailers and light commercial vehicles;
trailers;
light commercial vehicles and heavy commercial vehicles, such as buses and coaches;
trams;
cargo trailers;
bicycles;
horses; and
cabot trailers.
EU Member States must also ensure that:
the type approval process is transparent and free of charge;
the information provided is accurate and up-to-date;
there is no discrimination based on nationality, religion, race, colour, sex, ethnic origin, gender, age, disability, sexual orientation, age of the driver, disability or sexual orientation.
Manufacturers and importers must provide the European Commission with all relevant information on type approval procedures, including:
type of vehicle;
type approval and type-related information;
all information required for fitting parts or equipment on the vehicle; and information on maintenance and repair and maintenance;
information on the type of the vehicle.
Member States must inform the Commission and the European Parliament and the Council of any changes to the type approval procedure.
In addition, the Commission must:
make available to the public all the information required to obtain type approval;
provide the Commission with a report every 2 years on the operation of the system of access to vehicle type approval and on the maintenance information.
Report
The Commission must present a report to the Council on the application of the regulation by 2 July 2011.
FROM WHEN DOES THE RECOMMUST BE APPLY?
The Regulation applies from 2 July 2010.
BACKGROUND
For more information, see:
Types of vehicles and trailers (European Commission).
KEY TERMS
* Motor vehicles: vehicles designed and built to carry out a variety of tasks such as:
transport, including the carriage of goods, passengers, trailers, trailers and goods weighing more than 2 tonnes;
machinery, including parts and equipment;
equipment, including spare parts and spare parts;
vehicle maintenance, including repairs and maintenance.
* Light commercial vehicles: trucks, buses and cabs, including trailers, buses, cabs and coaches.
MAIN DOCUMENT
Council Regulation (Euratom), Euratom, of 29 June 2010, on the approximation of certain laws and regulations of Member States concerning type approval (OJ L 136, 30.6.2010, pp. 1-8)
Successive amendments to Regulation (EU, Euromatom, EC) No 550/2010 have been incorporated into the original text. This consolidated version is of documentary value only.

Summary 167:
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 596/2004 on substances authorised to be placed on the European Union market
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It aims to protect human life and health by:
ensuring that substances that have been authorised by EU countries’ food safety authorities to be sold on the EU market are not placed on a list that is determined by the EU’s law on food safety;
establishing a European Food Safety Authority (EFSA).
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to substances that are authorised by each sectoral food law in each EU country.
It does not apply to substances which have not been authorised in the EU.
EU countries may exclude substances from the EU list if they consider that they pose a risk to human life or health.
Rules for the application procedure
The European Commission must submit an application to the EFSA for the authorisation of a substance to be put on the market. The application must contain the following information:
a description of the substance and its intended use;
a list of the EU countries in which the substance is authorised;
the conditions under which the substances may be placed.
The application must be made available to EU countries by the Commission.
If the Commission receives a valid application, it must ensure that the substances on the list comply with the conditions laid down in the regulation. If not, the Commission must inform the applicant of the reasons for its decision to reject the application.
An EFSA must give its opinion within 9 months of receipt of the application and provide the applicant with all the necessary information.
FROM WHEN DOES THE RECOMMUSTOMMENDATION APPLACE
This regulation applies from 1 January 2005.
BACKGROUND
The EFSA is responsible for ensuring that substances which are not authorised in EU countries are placed on an EU market.
For more information, see:
‘Food Safety Authority’ on the Commission's website.
MAIN DOCUMENT
Council Regulation (EC, Euratom) No 550/2004 of 20 December 2004 on substances that may be authorised to place on the Community market
REFERENCES

Summary 168:
Rules on accreditation, market surveillance, controls of products from non-EU countries and the CE marking (until 31 December 2020)
Rules on accredited products, controls and market surveillance
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 596/2006 — rules on the application of the European conformity assessment system
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It aims to ensure that products from outside the European Union (EU) are subject to the EU’s conformity assessment and accreditation system.
It lays down rules for the accreditation of products and the control of products imported into the EU.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to all products which are intended for sale in the EU, whether they are new or second-hand. It does not apply to products which have been manufactured in another EU country and which have not yet been certified as being compliant with the relevant EU legislation.
EU countries must establish, implement and periodically update their market surveillance programmes. These must take account of established principles of risk assessment, complaints and other information. They must also ensure that their competent authorities participate fully in those activities.
Market surveillance
The European Commission must organise and carry out market surveillance to identify products presenting a serious risk to the health and safety of consumers and to the environment.
The Commission must communicate regularly to EU countries the results of market surveillance activities. It must also inform the European Parliament, the Council, the European Economic and Social Committee and the Committee of the Regions of the measures taken by EU countries to prevent, detect and respond to any serious risks to public health and the environment and the safety of the products are posing.
FROM WHEN DOES THE RECOMMUSTOMING DOCUMENTRYE DOCUMENTS
 
Council Regulation (EC, Euratom) No 550/2006 of 29 June 2006 laying down rules on market surveillance (OJ L 183, 30.7.2006, pp. 1-8)
Successive amendments to Regulation (Euratom) 2006/475/EC have been incorporated into the original text. This consolidated version is of documentary value only.

Summary 169:
EU-Iceland agreement on extradition for the purpose of prosecution or execution of sentences between EU and non-EU countries (OJ L 183, 29.10.2014, pp. 1-2)
EU-Norway agreement on extraditable offences
SUMMARY OF:
Agreement on extradition between the EU and the EU countries and the Kingdom of Norway and the Republic of Iceland
Decision (EU) 2015/852 concluding the Agreement on extradition
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE AGREEMENT AND THE DECISION?
The agreement aims to improve, in accordance with the provisions of the Convention on Extraditable Justice between the European Union and the European Community (now the EU), the surrender for prosecution and execution of sentence between, on the one hand, the Member States and Norway and Iceland.
The decision concludes the agreement on behalf of the EU.
KEY POINTS
The aim of the agreement is to:
improve, in particular, the surrender procedure;
ensure that the arrest warrant issued by the issuing country is executed;
promote cooperation between the authorities of the issuing and executing countries;
facilitate the exchange of information and information on the execution of the warrant;
reduce the time and costs involved;
improve cooperation between judicial authorities;
provide for the protection of the rights of the victims of criminal offences;
encourage cooperation in criminal matters between the countries concerned;
contribute to the fight against organised crime and terrorism.
In addition, the agreement sets out detailed procedures for transmitting an arrest warrant and for executing it.
It also provides for:
recourse to the central authority of the executing country;
the right to a lawyer;
protection of the victim of a criminal offence;
a right to appeal against the execution warrant.
Procedure
The executing country may refuse to execute the warrant if:
there are grounds to believe that the person concerned is a flight risk;
there is a risk of serious harm to the safety of the public or to the security of the country concerned; or
the person concerned has committed a serious offence punishable by a custodial sentence.
If there are other grounds for non-execution, the execution must take place as soon as these grounds have ceased to exist. The executing country must immediately inform the issuing judicial authority and agree on a new surrender date.
When a person is arrested, the executing judicial authority must:
notify the country in which the offence was committed and inform it of the reason for the arrest;
take all necessary measures to ensure that the individual concerned is returned to the country where he or she was arrested;
immediately inform the competent judicial authority in the country of the offence for which the person is being held.
Where a person who has been arrested in another EU country is a national of an EU country, that country must also inform the EU country of which he/she is a citizen.
EU countries may also apply reciprocal measures in relation to offences committed in the territory of the other EU countries.
FROM WHEN DO THE DECISIONS APPLY?
Directive (EU, Euratom) 2016/856 of the European Parliament and of the Council of 11 December 2016 on the conclusion of the Agreement for extradition between Denmark and Iceland (see summary).
BACKGROUND
The EU and Iceland have signed a number of bilateral agreements on extradition, including:
the Convention on extradition of European Union nationals and nationals of Iceland and Norway;
The Convention on the Protection of the Rights of the Victims of Crime and the Prevention of Terrorism; and
the Treaty on the Functioning of Europe.
For more information, see:
The European Union’s extradition policy (European Commission).
KEY TERMS
* Extradition: the procedure by which an EU national is extradited from one EU country to another.
* Arrest warrant: an international arrest warrant is issued by a judicial authority of another country to arrest an individual who is suspected of committing an offence in another country.
ACT
Council Decision (EU), Euratom of 29 November 2015 on the signature, on behalf the European Economic Area, of an Agreement on the extradition of persons who are suspected of serious offences and who are subject to arrest warrants issued by one of the parties to this agreement.
RELATED ACTS
Council Regulation (EC) No 852/2014 of 27 June 2014 on the application of the Treaty on European Union to the Convention of 27 September 1996 relating to extradition of nationals who are the subject of arrest warrants and to the protection against terrorism and the prevention of terrorism, and repealing Council Regulation (Euratom) No 552/2004 on the protection from terrorism, as amended by Council Decision No 553/2004.
last update 14.02.2016

Regulation (EC) No 596/2004 on the free provision of assistance to passengers with disabilities on board the bus and coach
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It aims to improve the accessibility of the transport system for persons with disabilities and people who are reduced in mobility.

children;

people with disabilities;

passengers who are unable to walk or use a walker.

Summary 174:
Statistics on aquaculture
Statistics on the production of aquatic animals
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 788/96 on fisheries statistics
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It lays down rules for collecting and compiling statistics on the EU’s fisheries sector.
It aims to improve the quality and reliability of statistics on fisheries.
KEY POINTS
The regulation lays down the rules for the collection and compilation of fisheries statistics.
EU countries must collect and compile statistics on:
the production of eggs and eggs-producing aquatic animals in hatcheries and nurseries;
the number of species of fish and crustaceans produced in these facilities;
production by species;
types of production;
methods of production.
The statistics are based on the following categories:
production of eggs (e.g. eggs, embryos, live fish, eggs laid by juveniles, eggs produced in the wild, eggs and live fish) and juveniles produced in nurseries (eggs, eggs, juveniles, etc.).
The production of live fish (eggs, embryos and juveniles) is based on categories such as:
freshwater;
salinity;
saltwater; and
marine waters.
In addition, EU countries may collect statistics on production by species.
Each EU country must submit a report to the European Commission every 2 years on the basis of the data collected and compiled by the Commission. The Commission must publish the report in the Official Journal of the European Union (JU).
The Commission must also publish a report on the results of the collection of the statistics and on the methods used to compile the data.
FROM WHEN DOES THIS REGULTRYTS REGULATIONS APPLACE OF ENTRY INTO FORCE
   
The Regulation has applied since 1 January 2008.
BACKGROUND
For more information, see:
Fisheries statistics (European Commission).
KEY TERMS
* Aquaculture: the production and processing of eggs, eggs-forming aquatic animals and juveniles in a controlled environment for the purpose of on-growing.
* Hatching: the process by which eggs are produced and processed in a hatchery or a nursery.
ACT

Summary 175:
Fishing in the area defined by the Convention on the Conservation and Management of Fishery Resources (CCMCC)
Fishing on board vessels engaged in IUU activities
SUMMARY OF:
Directive 2014/33/EU on the implementation of the EU’s fisheries control scheme
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE DIRECTIVE?
It aims to prevent and combat illegal fishing on board fishing vessels.
It sets up the European Union Fisheries Control Scheme (NEAFC).
KEY POINTS
Scope
The directive applies to fishing vessels flying the flag of a European Union (EU) Member State. It does not apply to vessels registered in non-EU countries.
National authorities in EU Member States are responsible for enforcing the rules of the convention on the conservation and management of fishery resources. To that end they must assign inspection vessels and aircraft to the scheme.
EU Member States must:
ensure compliance with the rules laid down in the convention;
establish contact points for receiving notifications and issuing authorisations in accordance with Articles 24 and 25 of the regulation;
monitor and report catches of regulated resources;
carry out inspections and follow-up of infringements;
provide information to the European Commission, the European Parliament, the Council and the European Economic and Social Committee (ESC) on the measures taken to prevent, detect and combat IUU;
report to the Commission any serious infringements.
Rules of conduct
Member States must ensure that:
the competent authorities carry out inspections on board and inspection of vessels;
the vessel is accompanied by a competent authority;
inform the competent authority of the number and type of vessel and the number of persons on board, the vessel.
The competent authorities of the Member State in which flag the vessel and of the country in which the vessel is registered.
If an EU Member State suspects that a vessel is engaged in illegal fishing, it must inform the competent authorities in that Member State without delay. The competent authority may issue an authorisation to land or tranship the vessel to a port designated by the flag country.
Inspectors must not carry fire-arms.
Reporting of catches
The Commission must ensure the following:
reports on catches;
ensures that vessels are registered in a Member State that is party to the convention and that the vessel has been inspected;
publishes an annual report on the number, type and number of vessels inspected.
Reports
Each Member State must send the Commission a report every 2 years on the catches it has inspected. The reports must include:
details of the vessel, its master and the country of registration;
a description of the fishing vessel and its cargo;
information on the type and type and nationality of the person on board the vessel;
where a vessel has not been inspected in the previous 2 years, a report must be sent to the relevant authorities.
Monitoring
The European Commission must send a report to the Member States on the inspections carried out by the NEAFC inspectors every 3 years. The report must contain information on:
fisheries caught in violation of the relevant rules;
fishing vessels registered outside the convention area;
flag countries’ compliance with these rules; and
the number of vessel registered in another Member State which has been authorised to land and/or tranship a vessel in breach of the rules.
Report
Each year, the Commission must submit to the Council a report covering the period from 1 January 2015 to 31 December 2016.
FROM WHEN DOES THIS DIRECTIVE APPLY?
 
   
It has applied since 1 January 2014. Member States had to incorporate it into national law by 1 January 2016. It had to become law in their Member States by 31 December 2015.
BACKGROUND
The EU has been involved in the CCMCC since 2004.
For more information, see:
‘Fishery resources’ on the EU's website.
KEY TERMS
* Illegal fishing: catches of fish caught outside the Convention Area (the Convention Area).
* Fishing vessel: any vessel engaged in fishing activities that are not regulated by the convention.
* Vessel: any fishing vessel that is owned or operated by a non-governmental organisation.
MAIN DOCUMENT
Council Directive 2014/34/EU of 21 December 2014 on the Implementation of the European Fisheries Control System (EC) (OJ L 183, 31.12.2014, pp. 1-8)
RELATED DOCUMENTS
                                   Council Directive (EU, Euratom) 2015/852 of 29 June 2015 on the enforcement of the Convention of the International Court of Justice on the Regulation of the Law of the Sea and on the Enforcement of Certain Rules of Procedure in the Field of Fisheries (ECJ L 347, 30.6.2015, pp.).
Successive amendments to Council Directive (Euratom) No 852/2015 have been incorporated into the original text



Summary 176:
EU Ecolabel — rules on ecolabel (e-labeling of products) (until 31 December 2020)
European Union e-label (E-label) rules on ecodesign
SUMMARY OF:
Delegated Regulation (EU) 2019/852 — rules for the application of Regulation (EC) No 1980/2000 on the ecolabelling of products
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
   
 
It aims to improve the environmental performance of products by ensuring that they meet the essential requirements of the European Union (EU).
It lays down rules on the use of the EU Ecolabels (Ecolabel).
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to all products that are intended to be sold or used in the EU, whether or not they are intended for human consumption.
It does not apply to food, animal feed, cosmetics, pharmaceuticals, food additives, food-processing equipment, chemicals, medical devices or food additives.
Eligible products
Products must comply with the requirements laid down in Annex I of the regulation.
Products that are not covered by the regulation must be labelled with a ‘e-colabel’ label.
The label must be clearly visible and clearly distinguishable from other labels.
Manufacturers and importers must ensure that the label is clearly visible on the product and that the product complies with the relevant EU legislation.
Operators must also ensure that:
the label bears the EU logo;
the product meets the key environmental characteristics set out in Annex II;
there is a clearly visible label;
it has been tested and certified to ensure that it meets the relevant requirements;
in the event of non-compliance, the product is subject to a conformity assessment, and the results of the assessment are made available to the public.
Fees
The maximum annual fee for each product is set at EUR 200.
Small and medium-sized enterprises (SMEs) and operators in developing countries must pay an annual fee of no more than EUR 750.
Micro-enterprises must pay a fee of at least EUR 350.
In developing countries, small and medium enterprises and operators must pay at least € 750 per year.
FROM WHEN DOES THE LEGISLATION APPLY?
It has applied since 1 January 2020.
BACKGROUND
For more information, see:
The European Commission’s website on the European Commission's website on e-Labels (European Commission).
MAIN DOCUMENT

Summary 177:
Protection of medicinal products against mutagenic effects
Protection against mutations
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 596/2006 on the protection of medicines against mutagens
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It lays down rules for the granting of a certificate to medicinal products to protect against the effects of mutagenesis.
It codifies and repeals Regulation (EC, No 595/2005) No 1082/2004.
KEY POINTS
   
The regulation applies to medicinal substances intended for human consumption.
The protection granted is based on the principle of ‘mutatis mutandis’ (mutagenic effect).
It does not apply to products intended for use as a medicinal product.
A certificate must be granted for a period of no more than 5 years.
An application for a certificate must contain the following information:
the nature and nature of the medicinal product;
the name of the competent authority which granted the authorisation;
a description of the product and the circumstances under which it was placed on the market;
an application for an extension of the duration of the certificate.
Applicants must also provide a copy of the application and the particulars contained in the application, as well as the certificate itself.
If the applicant does not meet the conditions laid down in the regulation, the authority may refuse to grant the certificate or reject the application.
Application for the certificate
The application must be lodged not later than 2 years before the expiry of the period of protection. If the application is rejected, the applicant must pay a fee of €2,500.
Applications for an extended duration of protection
An extension of protection must contain all the information required by the regulation. The application must also contain the particulars referred to in Article 1 of the regulation and the certificate already granted.
Where the applicant fails to comply with the conditions set out in Article 2, the certificate may be refused.
In the case of an extension, the application must contain:
a list of the products for which the protection has been granted;
information on the conditions for granting the protection;
instructions on the application for the extension;
procedures to be followed in the event of a refusal to grant a certificate;
details of the applicant’s name, address and contact details;
conditions for the application to be made to a competent authority;
exclusions from the protection granted to products which are not medicinal products.
FROM WHEN DOES THE RECOMMENDATION APPLY?
Directive 2006/96/EC has applied since 1 January 2007 and had to become law in the EU countries by 1 January 2008.
BACKGROUND
 
For more information, see:
Mutagenic Effects of Medicinal Products on Human Health (European Commission).
KEY TERMS
* Mitochondrial disease: a disease caused by the genetic make-up of a substance, such as a bacterium or virus, which has the potential to mutate the human body.
* Mutagenic impact: the effect of the presence of a mutageneric effect on human health.
ACT
Council Regulation (EU) No 550/2006 of 20 December 2006 on the Protection of Medicines against Mutagenics (Codified version) (OJ L 183, 31.12.2006, pp. 1-8)
RELATED ACTS

Summary 178:
Convention on the enforcement of judgments in civil and commercial matters (Lugano Convention on the Enforcement of Judgments in Civil and Commercial Matters) (Lagano Convention) (OJ L 347, 29.12.1998, pp. 1-8)
Convention in the field of consumer protection
SUMMARY OF:
Decision 98/852/EC on the conclusion of the Convention in the area of consumer Protection
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE CONVENTION AND OF THE DECISION?
The convention aims to ensure that the courts of the European Union (EU) countries that are party to it have jurisdiction over judgments issued by a court in another EU country.
The decision approves the convention on behalf of the EU.
KEY POINTS
The Convention applies to all EU countries that have ratified the Convention. It does not apply to the EU countries which have not yet ratified it.
Jurisdiction
EU countries must ensure that their courts have jurisdiction to enforce judgments issued in their country of origin. The judgments must be classified and provided with an abstract.
Judges must be delivered in the country in which the judgment has been or is to be enforced. The judgment must contain the following information:
the nature of the judgment;
the judgment’s subject matter; and
the date of entry into force.
If the judgment is delivered in another country, the judgment may be enforced in that country, provided that that country has jurisdiction over the judgment.
Where a judgment has not been and is to enforce the judgment in the judgment must be brought before the court of the country where the judgment was delivered.
In proceedings in which a judgment was issued, the court hearing the action must apply Article 26 of the convention.
When a judgment is brought before a court of a country bound by the convention, that court must apply the convention in the case where it has been issued.
A judgment may also be brought against a person who has been convicted of a criminal offence or who is the subject of a civil or commercial offence. The court of that country must also have jurisdiction in that case. If the outcome of proceedings in that court depends on the determination of an incidental question of recognition that court shall have jurisdiction.
Consumer contracts
The courts of an EU country that has not ratified the convention have jurisdiction when a consumer contract is entered into. The contract must be entered into by the consumer in writing and the consumer must be informed of the terms and conditions of the contract before the contract is signed. The consumer must also be provided with a copy of all the relevant documents.
FROM WHEN DO THE DECISIONS APPLY?
 
The decisions have applied since 1 January 1998.
BACKGROUND
   
For more information, see:
‘Consumer Protection Convention’ on the European Commission's website.
* KEY TERMS
* Judgment: a judgment issued by an EU court to enforce a judgment in a court other than that of the court which has jurisdiction to issue it. It may be issued in any EU country, but only if that court is competent.
ACT
Council Decision 98/884/EC of 29 December 1998 on the approval of the Conventions in the Area of Consumer Protection (LUGAN Convention) [Official Journal L 347 of 29.11.1998]
RELATED ACTS
Council Regulation (EC) No 596/2004 of 29 June 2004 on the application of the International Convention in Civil & Commercial Matters (ICC) to consumer protection and repealing Council Regulation (EEC, Euratom) No 696/2003 (OCT) No 852/2003) [See amending act(s)].
